Question 345 (NWSM - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
A 57-year-old man complained to his physician of epigastric pain that was stronger at night and was temporarily relieved by food. Upper gastrointestinal endoscopy showed two small gastric ulcers, and a urease breath test was positive for Helicobacter pylori infection. The physician prescribed a triple therapy with omeprazole, clarithromycin, and metronidazole for 14 days, followed by omeprazole daily for 6 weeks. Which of the following statements best explains why this drug regimen is the first-line therapy for H. pylori-associated ulcers?

Options:
  Clarithromycin greatly enhances the bactericidal activity of omeprazole
  Metronidazole greatly enhances the bactericidal activity of omeprazole.
  Omeprazole is rapidly bactericidal against H. pylori.
✓ The regimen almost completely eliminates the risk of ulcer recurrence.
  The regimen can cure the ulcer in up to 70% of cases.

Explanation:
Eradication of H. pylori drastically reduces the recurrence rate of peptic ulcers (from >70% to <5% per year).

Question 346 (NWSM - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
A 70-year-old woman complained to her physician of obstinate constipation. The physician prescribed a laxative that acts in the colon by absorbing water into the fecal contents, thus promoting peristalsis about 1 or 2 days after administration. Which of the following drugs was most likely prescribed?

Options:
  Castor oil
  Docusate
  Magnesium sulfate
✓ Methylcellulose
  Sodium phosphate

Explanation:
Methylcellulose is a bulk-forming laxative that absorbs water, swells, and distends the colon to promote peristalsis, typically taking 1-3 days to act.

✓ Urine pregnancy test
  Virology
  Serum electrolytes
  Urinalysis
  C reactive protein level

Explanation:
In a female of reproductive age with amenorrhea (late dates) and signs of shock/acute abdomen, Ruptured Ectopic Pregnancy must be ruled out immediately with a Urine Pregnancy Test.

Question:

Her physical examination is normal except for mild abdominal distention and evidence of a peripheral sensory neuropathy. Complete blood count, serum electrolytes, BUN, creatinine, and liver enzymes are all normal. Gallbladder sonogram is negative for gallstones. Upper endoscopy and CT scan of the abdomen are normal. What is the best next step in the evaluation of this patient's symptoms?

  Barium esophagraphy
✓ Scintigraphic gastric emptying study
  Colonoscopy
  MR cholangiography
  Small bowel biopsy

Explanation:
The symptoms (nausea, vomiting, early satiety) in a diabetic patient with normal structural workup (endoscopy/CT) strongly suggest Diabetic Gastroparesis. A gastric emptying study is the diagnostic test.

Question:
A 54-year-old woman has had colicky right upper quadrant pain and nausea for the past week. On physical examination, she is afebrile. There is marked tenderness of the right upper quadrant. The liver span is normal. Her body mass index is 33. An abdominal ultrasound scan shows calculi within the lumen of the gallbladder, and the gallbladder wall appears thickened. The patient's gallbladder is removed by laparoscopic cholecystectomy, and shows faceted yellow colored calculi. Which of the following mechanisms is responsible in development of her disease?

Options:
  Antibody-mediated RBC lysis
  Ascaris lumbricoides within bile ducts
✓ Biliary hypersecretion of cholesterol
  Hepatocyte infection by HBV
  Ingestion of foods rich in fat

Question 353 (NWSM - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
Vomiting is least likely in acute poisoning caused by:

Options:
✓ Carbolic acid
  Oxalic acid
  Nitric acid
  Phosphorus
  Sulphuric acid

Explanation:
Carbolic acid (Phenol) causes rapid CNS depression and mucosal anesthesia, making vomiting less likely or occurring briefly before coma, compared to the severe irritation caused by strong mineral acids or phosphorus.

Question:

✓ Ascaris
  Enterobius
  Necator
  Strongyloides
  Trichuris

Explanation:
Ascaris lumbricoides is widely distributed in the soil and infects humans via ingestion. Many hookworms are also in the soil, but Ascaris is often used as the primary example of a soil-transmitted helminth.

Options:
  One
  Two
✓ Three
  Four
  Five

Explanation:
Due to the intermittent shedding of cysts and trophozoites of parasites like Giardia and E. histolytica, three serial stool specimens collected over several days are recommended for optimal detection.

✓ Strongyloides

Question 405 (NWSM - 2025)
================================================================================

Question:
A patient suffering from helminthic infestation was started on a drug that relieved the condition by causing the flaccid paralysis Of the worm. The paralysis may be caused by which Of the following mechanisms?

Options:
  Enhanced entry of calcium into the cell
✓ Hyperpolarization of nerve ending
  Inhibition of cholinesterase enzyme
  Inhibition of microtubule polymerization
  Stimulation of Acetylcholine at myoneural junction

Explanation:
Drugs like Ivermectin and Piperazine cause flaccid paralysis by inducing hyperpolarization (via chloride channels or GABA receptors). Praziquantel causes spastic paralysis via calcium influx.

Question 406 (NWSM - 2025)
================================================================================

Question:
A 35-year-old man has been diagnosed with gastroesophageal reflux disease. He has been visiting his GP for regular checkups. Regarding GERD which one Of the following is not a risk factor?

Options:
  High fatty food
  Caffeine
  Nicotine
✓ Cholinergic drugs
  Gastric out let obstruction

Explanation:
Cholinergic drugs generally increase lower esophageal sphincter (LES) tone and gastric motility, potentially helping GERD. Anticholinergics, fatty foods, caffeine, and nicotine relax the LES, exacerbating GERD.

✓ Supportive care with oral rehydration solution (ORS) and electrolyte replacement
  Anti-emetic medication for symptom relief
  Surgical consultation for possible complication

Explanation:
Non-typhoidal Salmonella gastroenteritis is typically self-limiting. The mainstay of treatment is rehydration (supportive care). Antibiotics are reserved for severe cases or immunocompromised patients.

Question 411 (NWSM - 2025)

Question:
A thirty-year-old unmarried, presented to the ED with pain peri-umbilical region shifting to RIF, continuous pain and no radiation. Her dates are late by one week. Its associated with nausea, vomiting and anorexia. On examination the patient is pale tachycardia, with a bp of 90/60mm of hg. On abdominal examination there is slight distended abdomen With tenderness all-over abdomen, there is marked guarding and rigidity on the RIF and pelvis region. What is the most important test to perform?

Options:
✓ Urine pregnancy test
  Virology
  Serum electrolytes
  Urinalysis
  C-reactive protein level

Explanation:
In a woman of reproductive age presenting with shock (low BP, tachycardia) and abdominal pain with a missed period, a ruptured ectopic pregnancy must be ruled out immediately. A urine pregnancy test is the critical initial step.

Question 412 (NWSM - 2025)
================================================================================

Question:
A 35-year-old power technician is found dead beside a transformer. The body shows a small circular crater-like lesion on the left thumb and extensive internal muscle coagulation. There are no external exit burns. Which of the following best explains this finding?

Options:
  Current passed through a non-conductive surface
✓ Alternating current caused tetanic contraction preventing release
  Lightning strike with flashover
  Low-voltage contact with prolonged exposure
  Direct current shock with single muscle jerk

Explanation:
Alternating Current (AC) causes tetanic muscle contractions, making the victim hold onto the source ('hold-on effect'). This prolonged contact allows for deep tissue heating and coagulation even without massive external exit wounds if the grounding is diffuse.

Question:

Options:
✓ Perform colonoscopy
  Advise tumor markers for colonic cancer
  Re-assurance and continue the medical treatment
  Operate and perform colectomy
  Avoid coloscopy

Explanation:
Following an episode of acute diverticulitis, a colonoscopy is recommended (usually 6-8 weeks later) to rule out underlying colorectal cancer or other pathology that may mimic diverticulitis.

Question 414 (NWSM - 2025)

Question:
A charred body is recovered from a house fire. At autopsy, soot particles are found in the trachea, and carboxyhemoglobin levels are 45%. What does this finding indicate?

Options:
  The victim died before the fire started
  The victim was dead when burning occurred
✓ The victim was alive when fire started
  Death due to postmortem burns
  Secondary smoke inhalation

Explanation:
The presence of soot in the lower airways and a high level of carboxyhemoglobin (COHb) indicates that the victim was inhaling smoke during the fire, proving they were alive when the fire started.

Question 415 (NWSM - 2025)
================================================================================

Question:
A male of 35 years was diagnosed t be suffering from Onchocerciasis and was started on Diethyl Carbazine. A few days later he presented with fever, tender lymph nodes and tachycardia. It was decided to stop the drug and put the patient on an alternative drug. Which of the following is the drug of choice for this patent?

Options:
✓ Ivermectin
  Levamisole
  Mebendazole
  Niclosamide
  Pirezipine

Explanation:
Ivermectin is the drug of choice for Onchocerciasis. Diethylcarbamazine (DEC) can cause a severe reaction (Mazzotti reaction) in these patients due to rapid killing of microfilariae.

Question 416 (NWSM - 2025)

Question:

  Stimulation of bicarbonate secretion by epithelial cells
✓ Reaction with hydrochloric acid in the stomach lumen
  Binding to necrotic ulcer tissue
  Reaction with pepsin in the stomach lumen

Explanation:
Antacids are weak bases that chemically neutralize gastric acid (HCl) in the stomach lumen to form salt and water.

Question 428 (NWSM - 2025)
================================================================================

Question:
A study of patients with ascites includes measurements of serum and ascitic fluid protein levels. The serum-ascites albumin gradient (SAAG) is calculated. Some patients are found to have a high gradient, along with splenomegaly. They are found to have serum albumin less than 2.5 g/dL Which of the following conditions is most likely to produce a SAAG greater than 1.1?

Options:
  Budd-Chiari syndrome
✓ Cirrhosis
  Nephrotic syndrome
  Pancreatitis
  Peritonitis

Explanation:
A SAAG > 1.1 g/dL indicates portal hypertension. The combination of portal hypertension (splenomegaly) and low serum albumin (synthetic dysfunction) is most characteristic of Cirrhosis.

Question 429 (NWSM - 2025)

Options:
  Hanging
  Throttling
✓ Traumatic (crush) asphyxia
  Choking
  Drowning

Explanation:
Traumatic (crush) asphyxia occurs when heavy weight compresses the chest/abdomen, preventing venous return, leading to facial engorgement and petechiae (masque ecchymotique).

Question 432 (NWSM - 2025)

Question:
A 36-year-old, G3, P2, woman , has worsening nausea and malaise for a week. On physical examination her sclerae are icteric. Her liver span is increased and the liver edge is tender. She is at 16 weeks' gestation. Laboratory studies show her serum AST is 495 U/L and ALT is 538 U/L. She recovers and hepatic function returns to normal, but spontaneous abortion occurs at 18 weeks. ✓ Hepatitis E virus (HEV)

Question 433 (NWSM - 2025)
================================================================================

Question:
A welder receives a high-voltage electric shock and survives. Over the next few days, he develops progressive gangrene of the affected limb without initial blistering or charring. The most likely mechanism is:

Options:
  Heat coagulation of skin
✓ Deep tissue necrosis due to vascular spasm
  Direct cutaneous burn
  Secondary infection
  Arc-induced superficial burn

Explanation:
High voltage current flows through low-resistance tissues like blood vessels, causing endothelial damage, thrombosis, and vascular spasm, which leads to progressive deep tissue necrosis and gangrene often sparing the skin initially.

Question 434 (NWSM - 2025)

A 40-year-old male has been the victim of hit-and-run accident. During a forensic interview, he narrates the details of incident that do not match eyewitness reports or evidence, claiming he saved a child from the scene. This behavior is indicative of

Options:
  Hallucination
  Delusion
✓ Confabulation
  Illusion
  Fague

Explanation:
Confabulation is the fabrication of false memories to fill in gaps in memory, often without the intent to deceive, common in conditions affecting memory like traumatic brain injury.

Question 438 (NWSM - 2025)

Question:
Enteric fever is a systemic illness characterized by fever, abdominal pain, and non-specific symptoms including nausea, vomiting, headache, and anorexia. The causative micro-organism involved is?

Options:
  Shigella
  Vibrio cholera
  Plasmodium
✓ Salmonella
  Bacillus cereus

Explanation:
Enteric fever (Typhoid fever) is caused by Salmonella Typhi or Paratyphi.

Question 439 (NWSM - 2025)
================================================================================

Question:
A 52 year old man has had a 4kg weight loss and nausea for the past 6 months. Upper gastrointestinal endoscopy shows a 6 cm area of irregular, pale fundic mucosa and loss of the rugal folds. A biopsy specimen shows a monomorphous infiltrate Of lymphoid cells microscopically. Helicobacter pylori organisms are identified in mucus overlying adjacent mucosa. Cytogenetic analysis shows t(l I ;18)(q21 ;q21) translocation. He receives antibiotic therapy for H pylori and the repeat biopsy shows the resolution of infiltrate. What is the most likely diagnosis?

Options:
  Autoimmune gastritis
  Chronic gastritis
  Diffuse large B cell lymphoma
  Gastrointestinal stromal tumor
✓ MALT lymphoma

Explanation:
The presence of a lymphoid infiltrate associated with H. pylori and the t(11;18) translocation is characteristic of MALT lymphoma. The fact that it resolved with H. pylori eradication confirms the diagnosis.

  Aspiration pneumonia
  Gagging
✓ Choking due to airway obstruction
  Smothering
  Suffocation due to asthma

The sudden collapse while eating and the finding of a foreign body (peanut) in the larynx is the definition of choking (airway obstruction).

Question 441 (NWSM - 2025)
================================================================================

Question:
A 41 -year-old woman who works as a tattoo artist has had increasing malaise and nausea for the past 2 weeks. On physical examination, she has icterus and mild right upper quadrant tenderness. Laboratory studies show serum AST of 79 U/L, ALT of 85 U/L, total bilirubin of 3.3 mg/dL, and direct bilirubin of 2.5 mg/dL. She continues to have malaise for the next year. A liver biopsy is done, and microscopic examination shows minimal hepatocyte necrosis, mild steatosis, and minimal portal bridging fibrosis. An infection with which of the following viruses is most likely to produce these findings?

Options:
  HAV
  HBV
✓ HCV
  HDV

Explanation:
Hepatitis C (HCV) is strongly associated with transmission via needles (tattoo artist) and has a high propensity to become chronic (symptoms lasting >6 months/1 year), often with mild histological changes initially.

✓ Peutz-Jeghers polyp
  Hyperplastic polyp
  Tubular adenoma
  Villous adenoma

Explanation:
The combination of mucocutaneous pigmentation (lips/mouth) and hamartomatous polyps in the GI tract is characteristic of Peutz-Jeghers syndrome.

Question 443 (NWSM - 2025)
================================================================================

Question:
In a clinical study, patients with infectious hepatitis, including viral hepatitis A, B, C, D, E, F, and G, are followed for 5 years. During that time, prothrombin time, serum AST, ALT, alkaline phosphatase, total bilirubin, and ammonia are periodically measured. A liver biopsy is performed each year, and the microscopic findings are recorded. Which of the following is most likely the best predictor of whether a patient with viral hepatitis will develop chronic liver disease that progresses to cirrhosis?

Options:
  Degree to which hepatic transaminase enzymes are elevated
  Length of time that hepatic enzymes remain elevated
  Presence of chronic inflammatory cells in the portal tract
  Presence of inflammatory cells in the hepatic sinusoids
✓ Specific form of hepatitis virus responsible for the infection

Explanation:
The specific viral etiology is the strongest predictor of chronicity. For example, HCV causes chronic disease in ~80% of cases, whereas HAV never causes chronic disease.

Options:
✓ Fortifying food

  Enhancing food quality

Question 450 (NWSM - 2025)

Question:
At autopsy, a 35-year-old man shows a horizontal ligature mark around the neck below the thyroid cartilage, with fracture of the hyoid bone and petechial hemorrhages in the conjunctiva. What is the probable cause of death?

Options:
  Hanging
✓ Ligature strangulation
  Smothering
  Throttling
  Choking

Explanation:
A horizontal ligature mark below the thyroid cartilage distinguishes ligature strangulation from hanging (which is usually oblique and higher). The fracture of the hyoid indicates significant force.

  Primary biliary cirrhosis

  Biliary atresia

  Diminished deep tendon reflexes

  Splinter hemorrhages

Question:
A 35-year-old woman on long-term oral contraceptive therapy is found to have a 6 cm liver mass during an evaluation for abdominal discomfort. Imaging shows a well-defined, hypervascular lesion without a central scar. What is the most likely diagnosis?

Options:
  Focal nodular hyperplasia
  Hepatocellular carcinoma
✓ Hepatic adenoma
  Hepatic Hemangioma
  Liver metastasis

Explanation:
Hepatic adenomas are benign liver tumors strongly associated with the use of oral contraceptives. They lack the central scar seen in Focal Nodular Hyperplasia (FNH).

  Iron deficiency due to poor diet

  Acute viral hepatitis
  Autoimmune hepatitis
  Gilbert's syndrome
  Hemochromatosis
✓ pancreatic head carcinoma

Explanation:
The lab profile shows a cholestatic pattern (very high ALP/GGT, mild AST/ALT) and ultrasound shows dilated ducts. In an elderly male, this is highly suggestive of Pancreatic Head Carcinoma obstructing the common bile duct.

  Mucosal ulceration and edema

Question 465 (NWSM - 2025)
================================================================================

Question:
A 65-year-old lady with a history of aspirin induced gastritis has now presented with severe hip and knee joint pain that is thought to be due to osteoarthritis. She now requires treatment with NSAIDS. Which of the following would be most helpful for the prophylaxis against recurrent Gl bleeding?

Options:
  Omeprazole
  Sucralfate
  Nizatidine
  Atropine
✓ misoprostol

Explanation:
Misoprostol (a prostaglandin analog) specifically replaces the prostaglandins inhibited by NSAIDs, providing cytoprotection. While PPIs are also used, Misoprostol is the specific pharmacological antidote for this mechanism.

Question:
A 60-year-old woman complained to her physician of obstinate constipation. Which of the following drugs was most likely prescribed?

Options:
  Castor oil
  Docusate
  Sodium phosphate
  Magnesium sulfate
✓ Methylcellulose

Explanation:
Methylcellulose is a bulk-forming laxative that absorbs water and expands, stimulating peristalsis. It typically takes 1-3 days to work.

Question:
A young boy from a rural community in Pakistan presents with pallor, fatigue, and poor school performance. His family uses human feces as fertilizer in their vegetable garden. Blood tests show microcytic anemia, eosinophilia, and low serum ferritin levels. Stool tests reveal occult blood. On clinical examination, the boy exhibits signs of malnutrition, pedal edema, and a persistent rash on his feet. Which worm infestation is most likely contributing to his condition?

  Schistosoma mansoni
  Enterobius vermicularis
✓ Ancylostoma duodenale

Question:

  MRI
✓ Scotch tape test

Question 469 (NWSM - 2025)

Question:
A public hospital in a developing country has limited funds to expand either the dialysis unit or the vaccination program. The dialysis unit would benefit 200 patients annually, while the vaccination program could prevent illness in 20,000 children. What type of economic evaluation would best guide this decision?

Options:
  Cost-Minimization Analysis
✓ Cost-Effectiveness Analysis
  Budget Impact Analysis
  Cost-Benefit Analysis
  Cost-Utility Analysis

Explanation:
Cost-Effectiveness Analysis (CEA) is commonly used to compare different health interventions by calculating the cost per health outcome (e.g., cost per case prevented or life saved) to determine the best use of resources.

Options:
  Cost benefit analysis
  Cost effectiveness analysis

✓ Cost utility analysis

Cost Utility Analysis (CUA) measures outcomes in Quality-Adjusted Life Years (QALYs), incorporating both quantity and quality of life.

Question 472 (NWSM - 2025)
================================================================================

Question:
A 28-year-old man presents to the ER after intentionally ingesting rat poison. Initially, he has abdominal pain, vomiting, and garlic-like odor on breath. After 2 days, his symptoms improve, but on the 4th day, he develops jaundice, bleeding gums, and altered sensorium. Which of the following best explains this biphasic course?

Options:
  Renal tubular necrosis
  Delayed fulminant hepatic failure
  Acute pancreatitis
  Hypoglycemia due to insulin release
✓ Myocardial necrosis

Explanation:
This describes Phosphorus poisoning (Yellow phosphorus), which classically has a biphasic course: initial GI irritation (garlic breath), a symptom-free period, and then delayed fulminant hepatic and renal failure. The option 'Delayed fulminant hepatic failure' is the clinical picture, but 'Myocardial necrosis' is also a feature. Given the specific context of 'jaundice and bleeding gums' (liver failure) and 'altered sensorium' (encephalopathy), the question likely points to the liver failure aspect. Wait, looking at the provided options, 'e' is myocardial necrosis, but 'b' is Delayed fulminant hepatic failure. The symptoms (jaundice/bleeding) are hepatic. Correct Answer is likely B. However, if the key marks 'e' for some reason related to shock, that's possible, but B is the textbook description.

Question:
A 30-year-old woman has suffered intermittent bouts of lower abdominal pain and low-volume diarrhea for the past 2 years. On colonoscopy there is friable mucosa from the rectum to the ascending colon, and a perianal fistula is noted. Biopsies are taken and on microscopic examination show acute and chronic mucosal inflammation with focal erosion. Her stool is negative for ova, parasites, and bacterial pathogens. Which of the following ongoing testing procedures is most useful for long-term follow-up of this woman?

Options:
  Abdominal CT scanning
✓ Biopsy screening for dysplasia
  Genetic mutational analysis for NOD2
  Serologic titers for Saccharomyces
  Stool cultures for microbiota

Explanation:
Patients with Inflammatory Bowel Disease (specifically ulcerative colitis or Crohn's colitis) are at increased risk for colorectal cancer and require surveillance colonoscopy with biopsy screening for dysplasia.

A 42-year-old worker in a thermometer manufacturing factory presents with irritability, tremors, and gingivitis. He also complains of excessive salivation. Which of the following best describes his condition?

  Saturnism (Lead poisoning)
✓ Hydrargyrism (Chronic mercury poisoning)
  Phossy jaw (Phosphorus poisoning)
  Ergotism
  Minamata disease

Explanation:
Hydrargyrism is chronic mercury poisoning (common in thermometer factories). Symptoms include tremors, gingivitis, salivation, and irritability (Erethism).

Options:
  Dexamethasone
  Dimenhydrinate
✓ Metoclopramide
  Ondansetron
  Pyridoxine

Explanation:
Metoclopramide is generally considered the second-line agent for hyperemesis gravidarum when first-line agents (like Pyridoxine/Doxylamine) fail. Ondansetron is also used but typically later or based on specific protocols.

Question:

  Adhesions
  Indirect inguinal hernia
  Intussusception
✓ Volvulus

Question 499 (NWSM - 2025)

Question:
A 60 year old man presented with history of progressive yellow discoloration of his skin, generalized itching, dark colour urine and pale stool for last two months. On examination he is deeply jaundiced and having a smooth globular mass in right hypochondrium. What is the most likely clinical diagnosis?

Options:
  Acute hepatitis.
  Biliary cirrhosis.
✓ Ca head of pancreas.
  Choledocholithiasis.
  Hepatocellular carcinoma.

Explanation:
Courvoisier's Law states that painless jaundice with a palpable gallbladder (smooth globular mass) is unlikely to be stones; it is usually carcinoma of the head of the pancreas.

Question 500 (NWSM - 2025)

Question:
A 40-year-old woman had been self-medicating for heartburn. The preparation she was using was a combination of magnesium hydroxide and aluminum hydroxide. Which of the following reasons best explains why many antacid preparations on the market contain a combination of these two antacids instead of a single product?

Options:
  To achieve a bactericidal effect on Helicobacter pylori
  To avoid antacid overdose toxicity
  To avoid interaction with other drugs given concomitantly
  To facilitate gastric emptying
✓ To decrease the occurrence of constipation or diarrhea

Explanation:
Magnesium salts cause diarrhea, while Aluminum salts cause constipation. They are combined to counteract each other's bowel side effects.

Question 501 (NWSM - 2025)
================================================================================

Question:
A female of 58 years has been taking warfarin since 5 years following a prosthetic heart valve insertion. She started complaining of constipation for which she was started on a drug by the physician. Two weeks later she presented to the medical OPD reporting that her INR value has increased for which she had to decrease the dose of warfarin. Which of the following drug is most probably responsible for the patient's condition?

Options:
  Bisacodyl
  Cascara
  Domepridone
  Ispaghula husk
✓ Liquid paraffn

Explanation:
Liquid paraffin (mineral oil) interferes with the absorption of fat-soluble vitamins, including Vitamin K. Reduced Vitamin K absorption enhances the effect of Warfarin, increasing the INR.

Question 503 (NWSM - 2025)
================================================================================

Question:
A fifty-year-old male, presented to the emergency department with a chronic history of altered bowel habits and left sided abdominal pain for the last once week, he has passed stools stained with blood on and off. On examination the patient is febrile, tachycardic and there is left iliac fossa swelling which is tender and hot. He is thoroughly resuscitated now what is the further management plan?

Options:
  Immediate laparotomy
  Barium enema
  Colonoscopy
✓ CT abdomen
  Flexible sigmoidoscopy

Explanation:
The clinical picture suggests diverticulitis with a possible abscess (tender/hot mass). Barium enema and colonoscopy are contraindicated in the acute phase due to perforation risk. CT abdomen is the diagnostic modality of choice.

Question 505 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
A 14 years old male is found to have multiple almost 120 colonic polyps and few almost 3 stomach polyps on colonoscopy and endoscopy respectively. His grandfather died of colonic adenocarcinoma. He has also some vision problem. What syndrome he is likely suffering from?

Options:
  Juvenile polyposis
  Peutz - Jeghers polyposis
  Hereditary non polyposis colorectal cancer/ HNPCC
✓ Familial adenomatous polyposis/ FAP
  Irritable bowel syndrome

Explanation:
Familial Adenomatous Polyposis (FAP) is characterized by the presence of hundreds (>100) of adenomatous polyps in the colon. Congenital Hypertrophy of the Retinal Pigment Epithelium (CHRPE) is a specific extra-intestinal manifestation (vision problem) associated with FAP (specifically Gardner syndrome variant).

Question:

Options:
  Stomach
  Biliary tract
  Rectum
✓ Appendix
  Liver

Explanation:
The histological description (nests of monomorphic cells, salt and pepper chromatin) describes a Neuroendocrine Tumor (Carcinoid). The appendix is the most common site for incidental carcinoid tumors found during surgery.

  Microscopic colitis

Question 509 (WMC - 2023)

Question:
A polyp resected from colon of 11 year old male mucocutaneous freckles has a lobulated contour with Christmas tree like appearance. On microscopy stroma of polyp is separated by arborizing network of smooth muscles with complex glands in between. What type of polyp this?

Options:
  Hyperplastic polyp
  Juvenile polyp
  Villous adenoma
  Inflammatory polyp
✓ Peutz-Jeghers polyp

Explanation:
Peutz-Jeghers syndrome is characterized by mucocutaneous pigmentation (freckles) and hamartomatous polyps. The microscopic appearance of smooth muscle arborization creates a characteristic 'Christmas tree' appearance.

Question:
A young patient presented with chronic gastritis along with megaloblastic anemia. His serum B12 and folate levels are in process. Biopsy of gastric mucosa has been seen. The most likely findings in biopsy should be:

Options:
✓ Atrophic mucosa of body and fundus only with intestinal metaplasia
  Noncaseating granulomas In the body mucosa
  Dense inflammation in antral mucosa with visible H pylori
  Eosinophils in antral and body mucosa
  Glandular hyperplasia in antral mucosa with regenerative changes

Explanation:
Autoimmune gastritis (associated with Pernicious Anemia) specifically targets parietal cells in the gastric body and fundus, leading to mucosal atrophy and intestinal metaplasia, while typically sparing the antrum.

Question 511 (WMC - 2023)

Question:
A 65 years old male smoker presents with right sided parotid tumor. Histological examination of biopsy reveals papillae lined by pink oncocytic cells with dense underlying lymphomacytic infiltrates in stroma. Which of the following is most likely diagnosis?

  Pleomorphic adenoma
✓ Warthin tumor
  Carcinoid/ low grade neuroendocrine tumor
  Mucoepidermoid adenocarcinoma
  Bronchogenic adenocarcinoma

Explanation:
Warthin tumor (Papillary Cystadenoma Lymphomatosum) is strongly associated with smoking and is histologically characterized by double-layered oncocytic epithelium resting on a lymphoid stroma.

Question 512 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
Which of the following are the characteristics of right sided colon tumor?

Options:
  It is not found in HNPCC patients in contrast of left sided colon cancers
  It doesn't differ significantly from left sided colon cancer in clinical presentation
  Late presents as metastasis in bone and always moderately differentiated adenocarcinoma
  Early presents with abdominal discomfort, change in bowel habits and obstruction as constricting mass and shows range of differentiation in history
✓ Lately presents with iron deficiency anemia as exophytic mass and mucinous or poorly differentiated in microscopy

Explanation:
Right-sided colon tumors typically grow as exophytic polypoid masses. They often present late with fatigue and iron deficiency anemia due to occult bleeding, rather than obstruction (which is common in left-sided tumors).

Question:
A 30 years old male presents with dementia, hemiballismus and deranged liver enzymes. On further evaluation its abdominal ultrasound shows cirrhosis of liver. His viral serology is negative. What is the most likely next finding in this patient?

  Anti mitochondrial antibodies in blood
  Central cyanosis

  Papillary cystadenoma
✓ Pleomorphic adenoma

  Chronic Hepatitis

Question 519 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
During the pathogenesis of pancreatitis which enzyme after activation from its proenzymes and clotting, kinin and compliment systems?

Options:
  Phospholipase
✓ Trypsin
  Elastase
  Alpha amylase
  Lipase

Explanation:
Trypsin is the central enzyme in the pathogenesis of pancreatitis. Once converted from trypsinogen, it activates other proenzymes (like phospholipase and elastase) and inflammatory cascades (kinin, complement, clotting).

Question 520 (WMC - 2023)

Question:
An outbreak of acute hepatitis in this month of July and August is traced to the mixing of sewage with drinking water. The patients had jaundice, arthralgias and low grade fever. Transaminases were markedly raised. None of the patients died during the outbreak, both were pregnant females. What is the likeliest cause of this outbreak?

Options:
  HAV
✓ HEV
  HBV
  HDV
  HCV

Explanation:
Hepatitis E Virus (HEV) is transmitted via the fecal-oral route (sewage-contaminated water) and is classically associated with fulminant hepatitis and higher morbidity/mortality in pregnant women compared to other hepatitis viruses.

  Drug induced hepatitis

Question 522 (WMC - 2023)

Question:
A department of pathology reviews pathology reports of colorectal adenomas over the past 15 years and correlates them with clinical data. What set of factors is the most likely to correlate with the risk of developing colorectal carcinoma?

Options:
✓ Polyp size, histologic size, severity of dysplasia
  Polyp size and anatomic location
  Patient age, polyp size
  Polyp size and gender of patient
  Patient age and histologic type

Explanation:
The malignant potential of an adenomatous polyp is primarily determined by its size (larger = higher risk), histological architecture (villous > tubular), and the severity of epithelial dysplasia.

Question 523 (WMC - 2023)

Question:
A 70 years old lady who is in case of colon cancer. On biopsy her cancer has invaded the muscularis propria two paracolic nodes are involved with no metastasis. What is the TNM stage of her Colon cancer?

Options:
✓ T2N1M0
  T1N2M0
  T2N2M0
  T2N1M1
  T2N0M0

Explanation:
Tumor invading the muscularis propria is classified as T2. Involvement of 1-3 regional lymph nodes (two paracolic nodes) is classified as N1. Absence of distant metastasis is M0.

Question 528 (WMC - 2023)

Question:
A 40 year old woman presents with a 2 months history of burning epigastric meals. The pain can be revealed with antacids or food. The patient also reports a recent history of tarry stools. She denies taking aspirin or NSAIDS. Laboratory studies show a microcytic hypochromic anemia. Gastroscopy reveals a bleeding mucosal defect in the antrum measuring 1.5 cm in diameter. An endoscopic biopsy shows that the lesion lacks mucosal lining cells and is composed of amorphous, cellular debris and numerous neutrophils. Which of the following is the most likely important factor in the pathogenesis of this patient's disease?

Options:
  Achlorhydria
  Acute ischemia
  Autoimmunity
  Gastrinoma
✓ Helicobacter pylori infection

Explanation:
The clinical presentation (peptic ulcer, melena) and biopsy findings (active ulceration with neutrophils) in a patient not taking NSAIDs is most likely caused by Helicobacter pylori infection.

================================================================================
Question 529 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
A 60 year old man presents to his physician because of progressive dysphagia, first to solid and then to liquids. Endoscopy reveals a large fungating mass 2 cm above the gastroesophageal junction. Biopsy of the mass shows that the glands have extended into muscular layer and contain large hyperchromatic nuclei. A diagnosis of esophageal adenocarcinoma is made. Which of the following conditions can result in the development of this lesion?

Options:
  Esophageal rings
  Esophageal webs
✓ Reflux esophagitis
  Scleroderma
  Sliding hiatal hernia

Explanation:
Chronic reflux esophagitis leads to Barrett's esophagus (intestinal metaplasia), which is the primary precursor lesion for esophageal adenocarcinoma.

================================================================================
Question 530 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
A WINDOW period in the hepatitis B serology means?

Options:
✓ When hepatitis B antigen disappear but hepatitis B antibody has not appeared yet
  When hepatitis B antigen disappear but hepatitis c antibody is not appeared yet
  When hepatitis antigen disappear but hepatitis c antibody has not appeared yet
  When HBV DNA disappears but hepatitis B surface antibody has not appeared yet
  When hepatitis B antigen disappear but hepatitis c antibody has not appeared yet

Explanation:
The window period in Hepatitis B infection is the interval between the disappearance of HBsAg and the appearance of anti-HBs. During this time, IgM anti-HBc is the only serological marker.

Question 531 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
In the intestines the fibrosis and bands is caused by which of the following disease.

Options:
  Typhoid
✓ Tuberculosis
  Ulcerative colitis
  Acute ischemic colitis
  Amebic colitis

Explanation:
Intestinal tuberculosis characteristically causes transverse ulcers which heal by fibrosis, leading to strictures and band formation.

Question 532 (WMC - 2023)

Question:
All are causes of acute pancreatitis except:

Options:
  Alcohol
✓ Insect bite
  Gall stones
  Biliary stricture
  Mumps

Explanation:
While scorpion stings can cause pancreatitis, a generic 'insect bite' is not a standard cause. Gallstones, alcohol, mumps, and biliary obstruction are established causes.

  Gastroesophageal area

✓ Antrum
  Lesser curvature

Which of the following is most sensitive and specific antibody for Celiac disease.

  IgG anti reticulin antibodies
✓ IgA anti endomysial Antibodies
  IgM anti reticulin antibodies

Question 538 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
In peptic ulcer, antacids are now primarily used for:

Options:
✓ Prompt pain relief
  Ulcer healing
  Preventing ulcer relapse
  Control of bleeding from ulcer
  Reduced side effects

Explanation:
Antacids provide rapid but short-lived symptomatic relief (pain relief) but are not first-line for ulcer healing compared to PPIs or H2 blockers.

Question 539 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
Which gastro-prokinetic drug produces extra pyramidal side effects?

Options:
  Domperidone
✓ Metoclopramide
  Cisapride
  Ondansetron
  Promethazine

Explanation:
Metoclopramide crosses the blood-brain barrier and blocks dopamine receptors, causing extrapyramidal side effects (EPS). Domperidone does not readily cross the BBB.

Question 540 (WMC - 2023)

Options:
  Prochlorperazine
  Metoclopramide
  Domperidone
✓ Ondansetron
  Promethazine

Explanation:
Ondansetron (5-HT3 antagonist) is the drug of choice for highly emetogenic chemotherapy like Cisplatin.

Question 541 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
Which of the following drug belongs to osmotic laxative?

Options:
  Caster oil
✓ Lactulose
  Magnesium sulphate
  Liquid paraffin
  Bisacodyl

Explanation:
Lactulose is a non-absorbable sugar that acts as an osmotic laxative. Magnesium sulphate is a saline purgative (also osmotic), but Lactulose is the classic example in this context. Caster oil/Bisacodyl are stimulants, Liquid paraffin is a lubricant.

Question 542 (WMC - 2023)

Question:

Options:
✓ Dietary fiber
  Liquid paraffin
  Bisacodyl
  Senna
  Caster oil

Explanation:
Bulk-forming laxatives (dietary fiber, psyllium) are preferred in IBS with constipation (IBS-C) as they are gentle and regulate bowel movements.

Question 547 (WMC - 2023)

Which of the following drug among anthelminthics can cause corneal opacities?

Options:
  Albendazole
  Niclosamide
✓ Ivermectin
  Piperazine
  Pyrantel pamoate

Explanation:
Ivermectin is used to treat Onchocerciasis (River Blindness). The reaction to dying microfilariae in the eye can lead to corneal opacities (Mazzotti reaction), though the drug itself targets the parasite causing the eye damage.

Question 548 (WMC - 2023)

  It is curative for hepatitis B
  It is curative for hepatitis A
  It is active orally

Explanation:
Interferon alpha is used in the treatment of Kaposi's sarcoma (associated with HHV-8) in AIDS patients. It is not orally active (must be injected).

Question 550 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
Drugs which undergo high degree of first pass metabolism.

Options:
✓ Have low oral Bio availability
  Have greater therapeutic effects
  Are primarily excreted in bile
  Are contraindicated in liver Disease
  Have zero order kinetics of elimination

Explanation:
High first-pass metabolism means a significant fraction of the drug is metabolized by the liver before reaching systemic circulation, leading to low oral bioavailability.

Question 551 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
A 58 year old woman is brought to the emergency department 4 hours after vomiting blood and experiencing bloody stools. The patient was diagnosed with alcoholic cirrhosis years ago. The patient subsequently goes into shock and expires. Which of the following is most likely underlying cause of hematemesis and hematochezia in the patient?

Options:
  Alcoholic hepatitis
  Ischemia of the gastric mucosa
  Mallory weiss syndrome
  Peptic ulcers disease
✓ Portal hypertension

Explanation:
Massive upper GI bleeding (hematemesis + hematochezia due to rapid transit) causing shock and death in a cirrhotic patient is most likely due to ruptured Esophageal Varices, a consequence of Portal Hypertension.

Question 552 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
A 58 year old woman presents with 2 months history of abdominal discomfort and dark stools. Physical examination shows pallor but no evidence of jaundice. Laboratory studies disclose a microcytic hypochromic anemia, with a hemoglobin level of 6.7 g/dl. A barium swallow radiograph reveals a "leather bottle" appearance of stomach. Microscopic examination shows diffusely infiltrating malignant cells, many of which a "signet ring" cells in the stomach wall. Which of the following is the most likely diagnosis?

Options:
  Fungating adenocarcinoma
  Gastric leiomyosarcoma
  Gastric lymphoma
✓ Linitis plastica
  Menetrier disease

Explanation:
Linitis Plastica is the macroscopic term for the diffuse infiltrating type of gastric adenocarcinoma ('leather bottle stomach') characterized microscopically by signet ring cells.

Question 553 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
A 56 year old obese female presents to ER after being found unconscious by her daughter. Paramedics report that the female is found in stuporous condition covered with vomit. On arrival at ER, she is clammy and her BP is 85/50 mmHg. Her serum amylase is raised. Which of the following is the most likely cause of hypotension?

Options:
  Alpha cell tumor of pancreas
  Ectopic pancreas
✓ Acute hemorrhagic pancreatitis
  Pancreatic adenocarcinoma
  Cystic fibrosis

Explanation:
Raised amylase, shock (hypotension), and vomiting in an obese female suggest Acute Pancreatitis (likely gallstone-induced). Severe/Hemorrhagic pancreatitis causes massive fluid sequestration and shock.

Question 554 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
A 45 years old man presents with malaise, anorexia, and Vomiting to emergency room. The physician notices slight jaundice. Blood examination shows marked elevation of ALT and AST with AST/ALT ratio of 2.5. alkaline phosphatase is near normal. Serum copper and iron are normal. Histopathologist reports show Mallory bodies in hepatocytes. Liver damage from which of the following diseases most likely accounts these findings?

Options:
  Biliary cirrhosis
  Viral hepatitis
✓ Alcoholic hepatitis
  Hemochromatosis
  Wilson's disease

Explanation:
AST > ALT (ratio > 2:1) and the presence of Mallory bodies are classic features of Alcoholic Hepatitis.

Question 555 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
A 65 years old male presents with complaints of right upper quadrant pain. He was diagnosed HCV 20 years back. He also gives a history of ill health, fever, decreased appetite and fatigue. Biopsy specimen shows presence of bile and atypical lymphocytes. Apart from CT scan and other tests which tumor markers you will order to support your diagnosis?

  Carcino- embryonic antigen
✓ Alpha feto protein
  CA-125
  CA 15

Explanation:
Hepatocellular Carcinoma (HCC) is a major complication of chronic HCV. Alpha-fetoprotein (AFP) is the tumor marker for HCC. (Note: 'atypical lymphocytes' in the question likely refers to tumor cells or inflammatory infiltrate).

Question 556 (WMC - 2023)

Question:
A 25 year old man had been experiencing intermittent diarrhea which, over years, progressed to severe diarrhea, alternating with constipation, rectal bleeding, and passage of mucus. Question 557 (WMC - 2023)

Question:

✓ Meckel's diverticulum

Question 558 (WMC - 2023)

Question:
A 42 year old obese woman presents with severe abdominal pain that radiates to the back. There is no history of alcohol or drug abuse. The blood pressure is 90/45 mmHg, respiration are 32 per minute and pulse is 100 per minute. Physical examination shows abdominal tenderness, guarding, and rigidity.   Alcoholic hepatitis
  Chronic Hepatitis pancreatitis
  Dissecting aorta aneurysm

Question 559 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
A 27 year old woman presents with a 9 months history of bloody diarrhea and crampy abdominal pain. Three weeks ago. She noticed that her left knee was swollen, red and painful. Her temperature is 38C (101F) abdominal palpation reveals tenderness over the left lower quadrant. Laboratory studies show moderate anemia with a hemoglobin level of 9.3 g/dl. Microscopic examination of the stool reveals numerous red and white blood cells. A diffusely red, bleeding, friable chronic mucosa is visualized by colonoscopy. The colon is subsequently removed which of the following is the most likely diagnosis?

Options:
  Adenocarcinoma
  Carcinoid tumor
  Crohn disease
  Pseudomembranous colitis
✓ Ulcerative colitis

Explanation:
Bloody diarrhea, diffuse continuous mucosal inflammation (red, friable), and extra-intestinal manifestations (arthritis) are characteristic of Ulcerative Colitis.

Question 560 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
A 2 years old symptomatic child has increased serum ALT and raised serum direct/conjugate bilirubin levels since birth. Diagnosis is?

Options:
  Crigler Najjar syndrome I
  Crigler Najjar syndrome II
  Gilbert syndrome
✓ Dubin Johnson syndrome
  Rotor syndrome

Explanation:
Dubin-Johnson syndrome causes conjugated hyperbilirubinemia. However, it typically doesn't cause raised ALT or symptoms in infancy. Neonatal Hepatitis or Biliary Atresia are more likely for 'since birth' with raised ALT. But among options, Dubin-Johnson and Rotor cause conjugated hyperbilirubinemia (Crigler-Najjar and Gilbert cause unconjugated). Raised ALT suggests hepatocyte injury, unlike pure DJS/Rotor.

================================================================================
Question 561 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
A 22 year old woman from India presents with a 1 week history of fever, malaise and nausea. The patient is 6 months pregnant. Physical examination reveals jaundice and right upper quadrant pain. Result of laboratory studies include serum bilirubin of 5.2 mg/dl (60% conjugated), AST of 400U/L, ALT of 492 U/L, alkaline phosphatase of 470 U/L, anti- HAV antibodies negative. HBsAg negative, and IgM anti hepatitis E virus (anti- HEV) antibodies positive. The patient is at risk for which of the following?

Options:
  Diabetes mellitus
✓ Fulminant liver failure
  Pulmonary thromboembolism
  Renal failure
  Sclerosing cholangitis

Explanation:
Hepatitis E infection carries a high risk of Fulminant Hepatic Failure (up to 20% mortality) in pregnant women, particularly in the third trimester.

  Hepatitis A and B vaccination

Question 566 (WMC - 2023)

Question:
A 25 years old obese male patient presented with deranged LFTs as under. S. BIL. 0.7 mg/dl (0.4-1 mg/dl) ALK. P04. 245 (150-350) ALT. 124 (25-40) Hep B&C. negative. What is the most likely cause?

  Wilson's disease
  Hemochromatosis

  Autoimmune Hepatitis
  Alpha-1 antitrypsin deficiency

Question 567 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
A 60 years old HCV positive patient for last 10 years with compensated cirrhosis presented with 5 months history of abdominal pain, ascites, generalized weakness and weight loss. His alpha feto protein levels are 450 ng/mL (normal values. 0- 40 ng/mL) what will be the most likely diagnosis?

Options:
  Esophageal varices
  Acute pancreatitis
  Ca pancreas
✓ Hepatocellular carcinoma
  Non cirrhotic portal hypertension

Explanation:
In a patient with long-standing HCV cirrhosis, the development of new symptoms (pain, weight loss, worsening ascites) combined with a significantly elevated Alpha-Fetoprotein (AFP > 400 ng/mL) is highly diagnostic of Hepatocellular Carcinoma.

Question 568 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
A 50 year old female presented with 8 months history of lethargy, weakness, jaundice and pruritus. On examination she has jaundice, xanthelasma and hepatomegaly. Her anti mitochondrial antibodies/AMA test is positive. What is the likely diagnosis.

Options:
  Chronic viral hepatitis
✓ Primary biliary cirrhosis
  Autoimmune hepatitis
  Wilson disease
  Hemochromatosis

Explanation:
Primary Biliary Cirrhosis (now known as Primary Biliary Cholangitis) classically presents in middle-aged women with fatigue, pruritus, cholestatic jaundice, and is strongly associated with positive Anti-Mitochondrial Antibodies (AMA).

Question 569 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
Which of the following is the gold standard test for patients suffering from gastroesophageal reflux disease.

Options:
  Upper GI endoscopy
  Barium swallow
  CT scan with oral contrast
✓ 24 hrs pH monitoring
  LES manometry

Explanation:
Ambulatory 24-hour esophageal pH monitoring is considered the gold standard for diagnosing GERD, particularly when endoscopy is negative or symptoms are atypical.

Question 570 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
A 45 year old male presents with chronic abdominal pain, bloating, and irregular bowel habits for the past 6 months. The pain is relieved after passing stool. The patient reports no significant weight loss or rectal bleeding. Physical examination and relevant laboratory tests shows no abnormalities. Based on the provided information. What is the most common diagnosis.

Options:
  Diverticulitis
✓ Irritable bowel syndrome
  Celiac disease
  Colorectal cancer
  Crohn disease

Explanation:
The clinical picture of chronic abdominal pain relieved by defecation, associated with altered bowel habits, and the absence of alarm features (weight loss, bleeding) fits the Rome IV criteria for Irritable Bowel Syndrome (IBS).

Question 571 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
A 34 year old male diagnosed to have H pylori associated peptic ulcer disease on upper GI endoscopy and biopsy. Which of the following is the first line treatment for him;

Options:
  PPI+ clarithromycin+ Metronidazole
  PPI + bismuth salts + clathromycin
  PPI + levoflovacin + Amoxicillin
  PPI + Amoxicillin + metronidazole
✓ PPI + Amoxicillin+ clarithromycin

Explanation:
Standard first-line triple therapy for H. pylori consists of a Proton Pump Inhibitor (PPI), Clarithromycin, and Amoxicillin (or Metronidazole if allergic to penicillin) for 14 days.

Question 572 (WMC - 2023)

  Cholelithiasis
  Liver abscess
  Pancreatitis
  Both a & b

Question 573 (WMC - 2023)

Question:
A 20 years old male patient presented with pain right hypochondrium plus high grade swinging pyrexia from the last one week. He has bloody diarrhea for 6 days which has responded to antibiotics. Most likely diagnosis is;

✓ Amoebic liver Abscess

Question 574 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
A 50 years old female patient has presented with pain in right hypochondrium with vomiting with 5 kg weight loss. On examination the patient is jaundiced and has a soft mass in right hypochondrium. Most likely diagnosis is;

Options:
  Mucocele of gall bladder
✓ Carcinoma of pancreas
  Acute hepatitis
  Gastric outlet obstruction
  Emphyma of gall bladder

Explanation:
Courvoisier's law states that a palpable, non-tender gallbladder (soft mass) in the presence of painless jaundice is unlikely to be gallstones. This clinical picture (jaundice + palpable GB + weight loss) strongly points to an obstructing malignancy, most commonly Carcinoma of the Head of the Pancreas.

  CT scan
  Ultrasound
✓ Carcino- embryonic level
  Barium swallow

Explanation:
Serum Carcinoembryonic Antigen (CEA) levels are used for the surveillance of colorectal cancer recurrence after surgical resection.

Question 576 (WMC - 2023)

First line investigation to detect Liver disease is:

  ERCP

  CT Scan
  MRI scan
✓ Ultrasound

Question 577 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
Barium swallow can help in diagnosis of all of the following lesions except:

Options:
  Narrowing of lumen
  Space occupying lesions
  Anatomical distortion
✓ GORD
  Pharyngeal pouch

Explanation:
While barium swallow can demonstrate reflux or hiatal hernia, it is not sensitive for diagnosing Gastroesophageal Reflux Disease (GORD) itself, which is a mucosal/functional diagnosis. It is excellent for structural lesions like pouches, strictures (narrowing), and masses.

  Ureteric stone
✓ Acute appendicitis
  Pelvic inflammatory disease
  Ectopic pregnancy
  Intestinal obstruction

Explanation:
Rebound tenderness and localized pain in the Right Iliac Fossa (RIF) are classic physical findings for Acute Appendicitis.

Question 579 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
Which of the following investigations should be performed for multiple perianal fistula?

Options:
  Ultrasound
  CT scan
✓ MRI
  Fistulogram
  Biopsy

Explanation:
MRI is the gold standard imaging modality for pre-operative assessment of complex or multiple perianal fistulas, as it clearly visualizes the fistula tract(s) and their relationship to the sphincter complex.

Question 580 (WMC - 2023)

  Anal carcinoma
  Colorectal cancer

Question 581 (WMC - 2023)

Question:

  Pancreatitis
✓ Left lower lobe atelectasis
  Pleural effusion
  Wound infection
  Acute gastric dilatation

Post-splenectomy patients frequently suffer from basal atelectasis (left lower lobe) due to diaphragmatic irritation and pain causing splinting and shallow breathing.

Question 582 (WMC - 2023)

Question:
Investigation of choice for gall stones.

Options:
  Xray abdomen
✓ U/s abdomen
  Ct abdomen
  Mrcp
  Ercp

Explanation:
Ultrasound abdomen is the most sensitive, non-invasive, and cost-effective investigation of choice for diagnosing gallstones (cholelithiasis).

Question 608 (WMC - 2023)
================================================================================

Question:
A village has a total of 100 under five children measles vaccine coverage in this age group is 60% (Assuming 100% efficacy). Following the occurrence of a measles case in a child after a visit outside, twenty-six children developed measles. The secondary attack rate of measles is:

Options:
✓ 65%
  40%
  50%
  45%
  100%

Explanation:
Total susceptible children = 100 - 60 (vaccinated, assumed 100% immune) = 40. Secondary Attack Rate (SAR) = (Number of secondary cases / Total number of susceptible contacts) * 100. SAR = (26 / 40) * 100 = 65%.

Question 627 (WMC - 2025)
================================================================================

Question:
A 52-year-old man with GERD develops dysphagia. Endoscopy reveals an ulcerated lesion in the distal esophagus. Biopsy shows mucin-producing glands infiltrating muscularis propria. What molecular abnormality likely initiated this transformation?

Options:
✓ TP53 mutation
  CDH1 inactivation
  BRAF V600E mutation
  RET proto-oncogene activation
  Barrett's metaplasia with intestinal-type columnar cells

Explanation:
The patient's history of GERD and the biopsy findings of mucin-producing glands (adenocarcinoma) in the distal esophagus are characteristic of esophageal adenocarcinoma arising from Barrett's esophagus. The molecular progression from Barrett's esophagus to adenocarcinoma typically involves the early inactivation of the CDKN2A tumor suppressor gene, followed by the mutation of the TP53 tumor suppressor gene, which is a late event promoting invasion.

Question 628 (WMC - 2025)
================================================================================

Question:
A 48-year-old man with long-standing hepatitis C has elevated alpha-fetoprotein. MRI shows arterial enhancement with venous washout in a 3 cm hepatic lesion. Most likely diagnosis?

Options:
  Cholangiocarcinoma
✓ Hepatocellular carcinoma
  Liver metastasis
  Hemangioma
  Hepatic adenoma

Explanation:
The combination of long-standing hepatitis C (a major risk factor), elevated alpha-fetoprotein (a tumor marker), and the characteristic imaging finding of arterial phase hyperenhancement with venous phase washout on MRI are classic for hepatocellular carcinoma (HCC).

================================================================================
Question 629 (WMC - 2025)
================================================================================

Question:
A 50-year-old woman's liver biopsy shows PAS-positive, diastase-resistant inclusions. Likely diagnosis?

Options:
  Wilson disease
  Hemochromatosis
✓ Alpha-1 antitrypsin deficiency
  Autoimmune hepatitis
  NAFLD

Explanation:
PAS-positive, diastase-resistant globules in hepatocytes are the pathognomonic finding for Alpha-1 antitrypsin deficiency. These represent the accumulation of misfolded AAT protein in the endoplasmic reticulum.

Question 630 (WMC - 2025)
================================================================================

Question:
A 60-year-old man with a 40-year history of smoking and regular alcohol consumption presents with progressive dysphagia for solids, unintentional weight loss, and retrosternal chest discomfort. Upper GI endoscopy shows an ulcerated mass in the mid-esophagus. Which of the following risk factors most likely contributed to his malignancy?

Options:
  Barrett's esophagus
  Obesity
✓ Smoking and alcohol use
  Achalasia
  HPV infection

Explanation:
The location of the tumor in the mid-esophagus, combined with the extensive history of smoking and alcohol consumption, strongly points towards esophageal squamous cell carcinoma. Smoking and alcohol are the most significant risk factors for this type of esophageal cancer.

Question 631 (WMC - 2025)
================================================================================

Question:
A 35-year-old man with a 10-year history of Crohn disease presents with progressive jaundice, fatigue, and pruritus. Liver function tests show elevated alkaline phosphatase and gamma-glutamyl transferase (GGT). MRCP reveals multifocal strictures and segmental dilatations in both intrahepatic and extrahepatic bile ducts. Which laboratory test is most likely to support the diagnosis of an associated autoimmune condition?

Options:
  Antimitochondrial antibody (AMA)
  Anti-tissue transglutaminase (tTG)
  Hepatocellular ballooning
✓ p-ANCA positivity
  Elevated alpha-fetoprotein

Explanation:
The patient's presentation with inflammatory bowel disease (Crohn disease) and cholestatic liver profile, along with MRCP findings of biliary strictures and dilatations ('beading'), is classic for Primary Sclerosing Cholangitis (PSC). PSC has a strong association with perinuclear anti-neutrophil cytoplasmic antibodies (p-ANCA).

Question 632 (WMC - 2025)
================================================================================

Question:
A 28-year-old woman presents with intermittent right lower quadrant abdominal pain, diarrhea, and perianal drainage. Colonoscopy shows patchy areas of inflammation with deep ulcerations and cobblestoning. Terminal ileum biopsies show transmural inflammation with non-caseating granulomas. Which of the following features helps differentiate this condition from ulcerative colitis?

Options:
✓ Skip lesions
  Crypt abscesses
  Goblet cell depletion
  Pseudopolyps
  Inflammation limited to mucosa

Explanation:
The key features described – perianal disease, skip lesions (patchy inflammation), transmural inflammation, and non-caseating granulomas – are all characteristic of Crohn disease and help distinguish it from ulcerative colitis, which typically involves continuous inflammation limited to the mucosa and submucosa, starting in the rectum.

Question 633 (WMC - 2025)
================================================================================

Question:
A 48-year-old woman undergoes abdominal imaging for nonspecific pain. CT reveals a 4.5 cm well-circumscribed mass in the liver. MRI shows a central stellate scar. Biopsy shows hepatocyte-like cells separated by fibrous septae. She has no history of liver disease or OCP use. What is the most likely diagnosis?

Options:
  Hepatocellular carcinoma
✓ Focal nodular hyperplasia
  Hepatic adenoma
  Metastatic adenocarcinoma
  Cholangiocarcinoma

Explanation:
A well-circumscribed liver mass with a central stellate scar on imaging in a middle-aged woman is the classic presentation of focal nodular hyperplasia (FNH), a benign liver lesion.

================================================================================
Question 634 (WMC - 2025)
================================================================================

Question:
A 50-year-old man presents with dull epigastric pain that worsens on an empty stomach and improves after meals. He has a history of chronic NSAID use for osteoarthritis. Endoscopy reveals a 1.5 cm ulcer on the anterior wall of the duodenum. Histopathology shows necrotic debris, fibrin, and chronic inflammation. What is the most likely underlying mechanism for this ulcer?

Options:
  H. pylori urease activity
✓ Inhibition of prostaglandin synthesis
  Autoimmune attack on parietal cells
  Zollinger-Ellison syndrome
  Ischemic injury

Explanation:
Chronic NSAID use is a major cause of peptic ulcer disease. NSAIDs inhibit cyclooxygenase (COX) enzymes, which leads to decreased synthesis of prostaglandins. Prostaglandins are crucial for maintaining mucosal defense mechanisms, including mucus and bicarbonate secretion and mucosal blood flow. Their inhibition makes the mucosa vulnerable to acid-induced injury.

================================================================================
Question 635 (WMC - 2025)
================================================================================

Question:
A 70-year-old man is evaluated for fatigue and change in bowel habits. Colonoscopy reveals an ulcerative, infiltrative mass in the descending colon. Biopsy confirms adenocarcinoma. Which of the following molecular alterations is most likely involved in early tumorigenesis in this patient?

Options:
  TP53 mutation
  MLH1 hypermethylation
  BRAF V600E mutation
✓ APC gene inactivation
  KRAS amplification

Explanation:
The classic adenoma-carcinoma sequence for colorectal cancer, particularly in the distal colon, is initiated by the inactivation of the APC (Adenomatous Polyposis Coli) tumor suppressor gene. This is considered the gatekeeping mutation that leads to the development of an adenoma, which can then progress to carcinoma through further mutations (like KRAS and TP53).

================================================================================
Question 636 (WMC - 2025)
================================================================================

Question:
A 2-year-old boy presents with intermittent cramping abdominal pain and vomiting. The mother reports passage of blood and mucus per rectum. On exam, a sausage-shaped mass is palpable in the right lower quadrant. What is the most likely diagnosis?

Options:
  Volvulus
✓ Intussusception
  Hirschsprung disease
  Appendicitis
  Meckel diverticulum

Explanation:
The classic triad of intermittent abdominal pain, a sausage-shaped abdominal mass, and 'red currant jelly' stool (blood and mucus) in a child is pathognomonic for intussusception, where one segment of the intestine telescopes into another.

================================================================================
Question 637 (WMC - 2025)
================================================================================

Question:
A 55-year-old male with fatigue and arthralgia is found to have hepatomegaly. Lab tests reveal elevated ferritin and transferrin saturation. Liver biopsy shows brown granular pigment in hepatocytes. Which histochemical stain would best confirm the diagnosis?

Options:
  PAS with diastase
✓ Prussian blue
  Oil red O
  Masson trichrome
  Alcian blue

Explanation:
The clinical presentation of fatigue, arthralgia, hepatomegaly, and high iron studies (ferritin, transferrin saturation) is highly suggestive of hereditary hemochromatosis. The brown granular pigment is hemosiderin (iron). Prussian blue is the specific stain used to detect iron in tissue.

================================================================================
Question 638 (WMC - 2025)
================================================================================

Question:
A 42-year-old woman presents with chronic diarrhea and bloating. She reports weight loss despite normal appetite. A duodenal biopsy reveals blunted villi, crypt hyperplasia, and intraepithelial lymphocytosis. Which of the following is the most likely diagnosis?

Options:
  Tropical sprue
  Whipple disease
✓ Celiac disease
  Ulcerative colitis
  Irritable bowel syndrome

Explanation:
The combination of malabsorption symptoms (diarrhea, weight loss) and the characteristic duodenal biopsy findings of villous atrophy (blunting), crypt hyperplasia, and increased intraepithelial lymphocytes is the hallmark of celiac disease.

================================================================================
Question 639 (WMC - 2025)
================================================================================

Question:
A 70-year-old man complains of progressive fatigue and shortness of breath. He also notes a sore tongue. Labs reveal macrocytic anemia and low vitamin B12. Upper GI endoscopy reveals thinning of rugal folds in the gastric body and fundus. Biopsy shows glandular atrophy with lymphocytic infiltrate and intestinal metaplasia. What is the most likely underlying condition?

Options:
  Menetrier disease
  Peptic ulcer disease
✓ Autoimmune gastritis
  MALT lymphoma
  H. pylori gastritis

Explanation:
This patient has pernicious anemia (macrocytic anemia, low B12, sore tongue/glossitis) caused by autoimmune gastritis. The autoimmune destruction of parietal cells in the gastric body and fundus leads to loss of intrinsic factor (required for B12 absorption) and achlorhydria. The biopsy findings of glandular atrophy and lymphocytic infiltrate are characteristic.

================================================================================
Question 640 (WMC - 2025)
================================================================================

Question:
A 65-year-old man presents with progressive weight loss and vague epigastric discomfort. Upper GI endoscopy shows a linitis plastica appearance of the stomach. Biopsy reveals signet-ring cells infiltrating the gastric wall. What is the most likely diagnosis?

Options:
  Peptic ulcer disease
  GIST
  MALT lymphoma
✓ Diffuse-type gastric adenocarcinoma
  Carcinoid tumor

Explanation:
The presence of signet-ring cells is the histologic hallmark of diffuse-type gastric adenocarcinoma. This type of cancer is characterized by a desmoplastic reaction that causes thickening and rigidity of the stomach wall, leading to the 'leather bottle' or linitis plastica appearance on endoscopy.

================================================================================
Question 641 (WMC - 2025)
================================================================================

Question:
A 53-year-old woman complains of worsening abdominal pain and diarrhea. She was recently treated with broad-spectrum antibiotics for pneumonia. Stool toxin assay is positive. Colonoscopy reveals yellow-white plaques over erythematous mucosa. Which of the following is the most likely diagnosis?

Options:
  Ulcerative colitis
  Ischemic colitis
  Crohn disease
✓ Pseudomembranous colitis
  Infectious colitis

Explanation:
The history of recent antibiotic use, positive stool toxin assay (for C. difficile), and the characteristic colonoscopic finding of yellow-white pseudomembranes are classic for pseudomembranous colitis caused by Clostridioides difficile infection.

================================================================================
Question 642 (WMC - 2025)
================================================================================

Question:
A 60-year-old woman with chronic hepatitis C presents with hematemesis. Exam shows ascites and caput medusae. Labs show low albumin and prolonged prothrombin time. What is the most likely cause of bleeding?

Options:
  Mallory-Weiss tear
✓ Ruptured esophageal varices
  Peptic ulcer
  Gastric cancer
  Erosive gastritis

Explanation:
The patient has signs of decompensated cirrhosis (ascites, caput medusae, low albumin, prolonged PT) secondary to chronic hepatitis C. This leads to portal hypertension, which causes the formation of esophageal varices. Hematemesis in this context is most commonly due to the rupture of these varices.

Question 643 (WMC - 2025)
================================================================================

Question:
A liver biopsy from a patient with autoimmune hepatitis shows dense portal and periportal lymphoplasmacytic infiltrate, interface hepatitis, and piecemeal necrosis. Which serologic marker is most specific for this condition?

Options:
  Anti-mitochondrial antibody (AMA)
✓ Anti-smooth muscle antibody (ASMA)
  Anti-tissue transglutaminase
  p-ANCA
  Anti-centromere antibody

Explanation:
The histologic findings are classic for autoimmune hepatitis (AIH). Anti-smooth muscle antibody (ASMA) is the most common and specific serologic marker for type 1 AIH, the most prevalent form of the disease.

Question 644 (WMC - 2025)
================================================================================

Question:
A 27-year-old woman with a 6-month history of bloody diarrhea develops migratory polyarthritis. Colonoscopy reveals continuous mucosal inflammation starting from the rectum. Biopsy shows crypt abscesses and mucosal ulceration. What is the most likely diagnosis?

Options:
  Crohn disease
  IBS
✓ Ulcerative colitis
  Diverticulitis
  Ischemic colitis

Explanation:
The key features of bloody diarrhea, continuous inflammation starting from the rectum, and crypt abscesses are characteristic of ulcerative colitis. Migratory polyarthritis is a common extraintestinal manifestation.

Question 645 (WMC - 2025)
================================================================================

Question:
A 68-year-old alcoholic develops severe epigastric pain radiating to the back. Serum amylase is 2,000 U/L. Two weeks later CT shows a 7-cm, thick-walled, fluid-filled mass adjacent to the pancreas. This structure is best described as:

Options:
  Abscess lined by neutrophils
✓ Pseudocyst lacking an epithelial lining
  True cyst lined by ductal epithelium
  Mucinous cystic neoplasm with ovarian-type stroma
  Serous microcystic adenoma

Explanation:
The development of a fluid collection following an episode of acute pancreatitis (suggested by the history of alcoholism, epigastric pain, and high amylase) is a classic presentation of a pancreatic pseudocyst. A pseudocyst is distinguished from a true cyst by its wall, which is formed by fibrous and granulation tissue rather than a true epithelial lining.

Question 646 (WMC - 2025)
================================================================================

Question:
A 70-year-old smoker develops persistent painless swelling of the left parotid gland. MRI shows a 3 cm heterogeneous mass; biopsy reveals a mixture of squamoid cells, mucus-producing cells, and intermediate cells with t(11;19)(q21;p13) translocation. The tumor is:

Options:
  Pleomorphic adenoma
✓ Mucoepidermoid carcinoma
  Warthin tumor
  Acinic-cell carcinoma
  Oncocytoma

Explanation:
Mucoepidermoid carcinoma is the most common malignant salivary gland tumor. The histologic description of a mix of squamous (squamoid), mucus-producing, and intermediate cells is characteristic. The t(11;19) translocation, resulting in the MECT1-MAML2 fusion gene, is a specific molecular marker for this tumor.

Question 647 (WMC - 2025)
================================================================================

Question:
A 29-year-old woman with Helicobacter pylori gastritis develops a sharply punched-out 1.5 cm ulcer in the duodenal bulb. Which factor provides the strongest mucosal protection at this site?

Options:
  Reduction of mucosal blood flow
  Acidic gastric secretion
✓ Bicarbonate secretion from Brunner glands
  Activation of pepsinogen
  Secretion of interleukin-8 by foveolar cells

Explanation:
Brunner's glands are located in the submucosa of the duodenum. Their primary function is to secrete an alkaline mucus rich in bicarbonate. This secretion is crucial for neutralizing the acidic chyme coming from the stomach, thereby protecting the duodenal mucosa from acid-peptic injury.

Question 648 (WMC - 2025)
================================================================================

Question:
An elderly patient develops rapid-onset bloody diarrhea after eating under-cooked chicken. Stool culture grows motile Gram-negative curved rods at 42 °C. Which extra-intestinal complication is most classically linked to this pathogen?

Options:
  Reactive lymphogranuloma venereum
✓ Guillain-Barré syndrome via molecular mimicry
  Polyarteritis nodosa
  Hemolytic-uremic syndrome
  Endocarditis of prosthetic valves

Explanation:
The clinical scenario and culture findings (curved rods growing at 42°C) are classic for Campylobacter jejuni infection. C. jejuni is the most common antecedent infection leading to Guillain-Barré syndrome (GBS), an autoimmune demyelinating neuropathy. The mechanism is thought to be molecular mimicry between lipooligosaccharides on the bacterial surface and gangliosides on human peripheral nerves.

Question 649 (WMC - 2025)
================================================================================

Question:
A 50-year-old obese woman has colicky RUQ pain. Ultrasound shows multiple radiopaque gallstones. Which composition is most likely?

Options:
  Pure bilirubinate (black) stones
✓ Mixed cholesterol stones with calcium salts
  Pure cholesterol stones (> 95 % cholesterol)
  Brown pigment stones with fatty acid soaps
  Stones rich in hemoglobin S fragments

Explanation:
The most common type of gallstones in the Western world, associated with risk factors like obesity (the '4 Fs': female, fat, forty, fertile), are cholesterol stones. Pure cholesterol stones are radiolucent. For stones to be radiopaque, they must contain a significant amount of calcium salts (carbonate, phosphate, bilirubinate). Therefore, mixed cholesterol stones with calcification are the most likely diagnosis.

Question 650 (WMC - 2025)
================================================================================

Question:
A 45-year-old female HCV positive patient notes painless fresh red blood on toilet paper. Anoscopy shows dilated venous cushions above the dentate line. Histology demonstrates mucosa lined by columnar epithelium with engorged submucosal veins. Which risk factor most directly contributed?

Options:
✓ Portal hypertension from cirrhosis
  HPV-16 infection
  Chronic laxative abuse
  Low-fiber diet
  Iron-deficiency anemia

Explanation:
The patient has HCV, a leading cause of cirrhosis, which in turn leads to portal hypertension. The description of dilated venous cushions above the dentate line is consistent with internal hemorrhoids. While common hemorrhoids are due to straining, in a patient with liver disease, they can be a manifestation of portosystemic shunting (anastomosis between the superior and middle/inferior rectal veins) due to elevated portal venous pressure.
